<p><b>Madonna Louise Ciccone</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted" title="/tʃ/ 'ch' in 'china'">tʃ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted" title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'">ɪ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted" title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted" title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted" title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'bode'">oʊ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted" title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted" title="/i/ 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></a></span><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span></span>; born August 16, 1958) is an American singer, songwriter, actress, dancer, and businesswoman. She achieved popularity by pushing the boundaries of lyrical content in mainstream popular music and imagery in her <a href="/wiki/Music_video" title="Music video">music videos</a>, which became a fixture on <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>. Madonna is known for reinventing both her music and image, and for maintaining her autonomy within the recording industry. <a href="/wiki/Music_criticism" title="Music criticism">Music critics</a> have acclaimed her musical productions which have also been known to induce controversy. Often referred to as the "<a href="/wiki/Honorific_nicknames_in_popular_music" title="Honorific nicknames in popular music">Queen of Pop</a>", she is cited as an influence among <a href="/wiki/List_of_artists_influenced_by_Madonna" title="List of artists influenced by Madonna">other artists</a> around the world.</p>
<p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Bay_City,_Michigan" title="Bay City, Michigan">Bay City, Michigan</a>, Madonna attended the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan_School_of_Music,_Theatre_%26_Dance" title="University of Michigan School of Music, Theatre &amp; Dance">University of Michigan School of Music, Theatre &amp; Dance</a> before moving to <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> to pursue a career in modern dance. After performing in the music groups <a href="/wiki/Breakfast_Club_(band)" title="Breakfast Club (band)">Breakfast Club</a> and Emmy, she signed with <a href="/wiki/Sire_Records" title="Sire Records">Sire Records</a> (an affiliate of <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros. Records</a>) in 1982 and released her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madonna_(album)" title="Madonna (album)">self-titled debut album</a> the following year. She followed it with a series of commercially successful albums, including the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> winners <i><a href="/wiki/Ray_of_Light" title="Ray of Light">Ray of Light</a></i> (1998) and <i><a href="/wiki/Confessions_on_a_Dance_Floor" title="Confessions on a Dance Floor">Confessions on a Dance Floor</a></i> (2005). Throughout her career, she has written and produced most of her songs, with many of them reaching number one on the record charts, including "<a href="/wiki/Like_a_Virgin_(song)" title="Like a Virgin (song)">Like a Virgin</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Into_the_Groove" title="Into the Groove">Into the Groove</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Papa_Don%27t_Preach" title="Papa Don't Preach">Papa Don't Preach</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Like_a_Prayer_(song)" title="Like a Prayer (song)">Like a Prayer</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Vogue_(Madonna_song)" title="Vogue (Madonna song)">Vogue</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Frozen_(Madonna_song)" title="Frozen (Madonna song)">Frozen</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Music_(Madonna_song)" title="Music (Madonna song)">Music</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hung_Up" title="Hung Up">Hung Up</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/4_Minutes_(Madonna_song)" title="4 Minutes (Madonna song)">4 Minutes</a>".</p>
<p>Madonna's popularity was further enhanced by her film roles; she won a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe Award</a> for Best Actress for <i><a href="/wiki/Evita_(1996_film)" title="Evita (1996 film)">Evita</a></i> (1996) while most of her other films have been panned by critics. Her other ventures include fashion design, writing children's books, and filmmaking. She has been acclaimed as a businesswoman, particularly after she founded entertainment company <a href="/wiki/Maverick_(company)" title="Maverick (company)">Maverick</a> (including the label <a href="/wiki/Maverick_Records" title="Maverick Records">Maverick Records</a>) in 1992 as a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Time_Warner" title="Time Warner">Time Warner</a>. In 2007, she signed an unprecedented US $120 million <a href="/wiki/360_deal" title="360 deal">360 deal</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Live_Nation" title="Live Nation">Live Nation</a>.</p>
<p>Madonna has sold more than 300 million records worldwide and is recognized as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">best-selling female recording artist of all time</a> by <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a></i>. According to the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA), she is the best-selling female rock artist of the 20th century and <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists_in_the_United_States" title="List of best-selling music artists in the United States">the second best-selling female artist in the United States</a>, with 64.5 million <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">certified</a> albums. <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> ranked her at number two, behind only <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>, on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100_50th_Anniversary_Charts" title="Billboard Hot 100 50th Anniversary Charts"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 All-Time Top Artists</a>, making her the most successful solo artist in the history of American singles chart. The magazine also declared her as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_concert_tours" title="List of highest-grossing concert tours">top-touring female artist of all time</a>. She became one of the five founding members of the <a href="/wiki/UK_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="UK Music Hall of Fame">UK Music Hall of Fame</a> and was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> in her first year of eligibility.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_career">Life and career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1958.E2.80.9381:_Early_life_and_career_beginnings">1958–81: Early life and career beginnings</span></h3>
<p>Madonna Louise Ciccone was born to a Catholic family in <a href="/wiki/Bay_City,_Michigan" title="Bay City, Michigan">Bay City, Michigan</a>, on August 16, 1958. She is the eldest daughter of Silvio Anthony "Tony" Ciccone and Madonna Louise Fortin (<i>c</i>. 1933 – December 1, 1963).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mom_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-mom-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Her father's parents were immigrants from <a href="/wiki/Pacentro" title="Pacentro">Pacentro</a>, Italy, while her mother was of <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French-Canadian</a> ancestry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Tony worked as an engineer designer for <a href="/wiki/Chrysler" title="Chrysler">Chrysler</a> and <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a>. Since Madonna had the same name as her mother, family members called her "Little Nonni". She has two elder brothers, Anthony (born 1956) and Martin (born 1957), and three younger siblings, Paula (born 1959), <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Ciccone" title="Christopher Ciccone">Christopher</a> (born 1960), and Melanie (born 1962).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thechild_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-thechild-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Upon receiving <a href="/wiki/Confirmation_(Catholic_Church)" title="Confirmation (Catholic Church)">confirmation</a> in 1966, she adopted <a href="/wiki/Saint_Veronica" title="Saint Veronica">Veronica</a> as an additional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Confirmation_name" title="Confirmation name">confirmation name</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> She was raised in the Detroit suburbs of <a href="/wiki/Pontiac,_Michigan" title="Pontiac, Michigan">Pontiac</a> and Avon Township (now <a href="/wiki/Rochester_Hills,_Michigan" title="Rochester Hills, Michigan">Rochester Hills</a>). Months before her mother died from breast cancer, Madonna noticed changes in her behavior and personality, although she did not understand the reason.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mom_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-mom-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Her mother was at a loss to explain her medical condition, and often began to cry when Madonna questioned her about it. Madonna later acknowledged that she had not grasped the concept of her mother dying.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madonna_family_in_their_vineyard_cropped.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="418" data-file-width="270" height="263" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Madonna_family_in_their_vineyard_cropped.jpg/170px-Madonna_family_in_their_vineyard_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Madonna_family_in_their_vineyard_cropped.jpg/255px-Madonna_family_in_their_vineyard_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e9/Madonna_family_in_their_vineyard_cropped.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Madonna_family_in_their_vineyard_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tony Ciccone with his wife Joan, pictured in 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Madonna turned to her paternal grandmother in the hope of finding some solace and some form of her mother in her. The Ciccone siblings resented housekeepers and invariably rebelled against anyone brought into their home ostensibly to take the place of their beloved mother. Madonna later told <i><a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (magazine)">Vanity Fair</a></i> that she saw herself in her youth as a "lonely girl who was searching for something. I wasn't rebellious in a certain way. I cared about being good at something. I didn't shave my underarms and I didn't wear make-up like normal girls do. But I studied and I got good grades..... I wanted to be somebody." Terrified that Tony could be taken from her as well, Madonna was often unable to sleep unless she was near him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mom_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-mom-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1966, Tony married the family's housekeeper Joan Gustafson, and they had two children: Jennifer (born 1967) and Mario (born 1968).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thechild_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-thechild-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> At this point, Madonna started to resent him for decades, and developed a rebellious attitude.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mom_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-mom-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> She attended St. Frederick's and St. Andrew's Catholic Elementary Schools, and then West Middle School. She was known for her high <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grade_(education)" title="Grade (education)">grade point average</a>, and achieved notoriety for her unconventional behavior, she would perform cartwheels and handstands in the hallways between classes, dangle by her knees from the <a href="/wiki/Jungle_gym" title="Jungle gym">monkey bars</a> during recess, and pull up her skirt during class—all so that the boys could see her underwear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tarabio_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-tarabio-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Madonna later attended <a href="/wiki/Rochester_Adams_High_School" title="Rochester Adams High School">Rochester Adams High School</a> where she became a straight-A student and a member of the cheerleading squad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> After graduating, she received a dance scholarship to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan_School_of_Music,_Theatre_%26_Dance" title="University of Michigan School of Music, Theatre &amp; Dance">University of Michigan School of Music, Theatre &amp; Dance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> She convinced her father to allow her to take ballet lessons<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> and was persuaded by Christopher Flynn, her ballet teacher, to pursue a career in dance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1978, she dropped out of college and relocated to New York City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> She had little money and worked as a waitress at <a href="/wiki/Dunkin%27_Donuts" title="Dunkin' Donuts">Dunkin' Donuts</a> and with <a href="/wiki/Modern_dance" title="Modern dance">modern dance</a> troupes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna said of her move to New York, "It was the first time I'd ever taken a plane, the first time I'd ever gotten a taxi cab. I came here with $35 in my pocket. It was the bravest thing I'd ever done."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> She started to work as a backup dancer for other established artists. During a late night, Madonna was returning from a rehearsal, when a pair of men held her at knifepoint and forced her to perform <a href="/wiki/Fellatio" title="Fellatio">fellatio</a>. Madonna later commented that "the episode was a taste of my weakness, it showed me that I still could not save myself in spite of all the strong-girl show. I could never forget it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>While performing as a backup singer and dancer for the French disco artist <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Hernandez" title="Patrick Hernandez">Patrick Hernandez</a> on his 1979 world tour, Madonna became romantically involved with musician Dan Gilroy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tarabio_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-tarabio-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goldmine_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-goldmine-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Together, they formed her first <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> band, the <a href="/wiki/Breakfast_Club_(band)" title="Breakfast Club (band)">Breakfast Club</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> for which Madonna sang and played drums and guitar. In 1980<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thechild_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-thechild-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> or 1981<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rolling_Biography_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Biography-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> she left Breakfast Club and, with her former boyfriend <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Bray" title="Stephen Bray">Stephen Bray</a> as drummer, formed the band Emmy. The two began writing songs together and Madonna later decide to market herself as a solo act.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-breakfastclub_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-breakfastclub-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Their music impressed DJ and record producer <a href="/wiki/Mark_Kamins" title="Mark Kamins">Mark Kamins</a> who arranged a meeting between Madonna and <a href="/wiki/Sire_Records" title="Sire Records">Sire Records</a> founder <a href="/wiki/Seymour_Stein" title="Seymour Stein">Seymour Stein</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rolling_Biography_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Biography-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1982.E2.80.9385:_Madonna.2C_Like_a_Virgin.2C_and_first_marriage">1982–85: <i>Madonna</i>, <i>Like a Virgin</i>, and first marriage</span></h3>
<p>After Madonna signed a <a href="/wiki/Single_(music)" title="Single (music)">singles</a> deal with Sire, her debut single, "<a href="/wiki/Everybody_(Madonna_song)" title="Everybody (Madonna song)">Everybody</a>", was released in October 1982, and the second one, "<a href="/wiki/Burning_Up_(Madonna_song)" title="Burning Up (Madonna song)">Burning Up</a>", in March 1983. Both became big club hits in the United States, reaching number three on <a href="/wiki/Hot_Dance_Club_Songs" title="Hot Dance Club Songs">Hot Dance Club Songs</a> chart compiled by <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> magazine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> After this success, she started developing her debut album, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madonna_(album)" title="Madonna (album)">Madonna</a></i>, which was primarily produced by <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Lucas" title="Reggie Lucas">Reggie Lucas</a>, a Warner Bros. producer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tara1_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-tara1-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> However, she was not happy with the completed tracks and disagreed with Lucas' production techniques, so decided to seek additional help. Madonna moved in with boyfriend <a href="/wiki/John_Benitez" title="John Benitez">John "Jellybean" Benitez</a>, asking his help for finishing the album's production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tara1_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-tara1-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Benitez remixed most of the tracks and produced "<a href="/wiki/Holiday_(Madonna_song)" title="Holiday (Madonna song)">Holiday</a>", which was her third single and her first global hit. The overall sound of <i>Madonna</i> was dissonant and in the form of upbeat synthetic disco, utilizing some of the new technology of the time, like the <a href="/wiki/LinnDrum" title="LinnDrum">Linn drum machine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moog_Taurus" title="Moog Taurus">Moog bass</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Synthesizer" title="Synthesizer">OB-X synthesizer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tara1_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-tara1-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was released in July 1983 and peaked at number eight on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> six months later, in 1984. It yielded two more hit singles, "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Borderline_(song)" title="Borderline (song)">Borderline</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Lucky_Star_(Madonna_song)" title="Lucky Star (Madonna song)">Lucky Star</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbalbums_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbalbums-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbsingles_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbsingles-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"I was surprised by how people reacted to 'Like a Virgin' because when I did that song, to me, I was singing about how something made me feel a certain way—brand-new and fresh—and everyone interpreted it as 'I don't want to be a virgin anymore. Fuck my brains out!' That's not what I sang at all. 'Like a Virgin' was always absolutely ambiguous."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—Madonna on the backlash for "Like a Virgin"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>Madonna's look and style of dressing, her performances, and her music videos influenced young girls and women and her style became one of the female <a href="/wiki/1980s_in_fashion" title="1980s in fashion">fashion trends of the 1980s</a>. It was created by stylist and jewelry designer <a href="/wiki/Maripol" title="Maripol">Maripol</a> and the look consisted of lace tops, skirts over <a href="/wiki/Capri_pants" title="Capri pants">capri pants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fishnet" title="Fishnet">fishnet stockings</a>, jewelry bearing the <a href="/wiki/Crucifix" title="Crucifix">crucifix</a>, bracelets, and bleached hair.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna achieved global recognition after the release of her second studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Like_a_Virgin" title="Like a Virgin">Like a Virgin</a></i>, in November 1984. It topped the charts in several countries and became her first number one album on the <i>Billboard</i> 200.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbalbums_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbalbums-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> The title track, "<a href="/wiki/Like_a_Virgin_(song)" title="Like a Virgin (song)">Like a Virgin</a>", topped the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart for six consecutive weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> It attracted the attention of organizations who complained that the song and its accompanying video promoted premarital sex and undermined family values,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> and moralists sought to have the song and video banned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Madonna came under further fire when she performed "Like a Virgin" at the first 1984 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</a> (VMA) where she appeared on stage atop a giant wedding cake, wearing a wedding dress and white gloves. The performance is noted by MTV as an iconic moment in VMA history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> In later years, Madonna commented that she was actually terrified of the performance. The next hit was "<a href="/wiki/Material_Girl" title="Material Girl">Material Girl</a>" promoted by the iconic video, which was a <a href="/wiki/Mimicry" title="Mimicry">mimicry</a> of <a href="/wiki/Marilyn_Monroe" title="Marilyn Monroe">Marilyn Monroe</a>'s performance of the song "<a href="/wiki/Diamonds_Are_a_Girl%27s_Best_Friend" title="Diamonds Are a Girl's Best Friend">Diamonds Are a Girl's Best Friend</a>" from the 1953 film <i><a href="/wiki/Gentlemen_Prefer_Blondes_(1953_film)" title="Gentlemen Prefer Blondes (1953 film)">Gentlemen Prefer Blondes</a></i>. While filming this video Madonna started dating actor <a href="/wiki/Sean_Penn" title="Sean Penn">Sean Penn</a> and married him on her birthday in 1985.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-secretlife_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-secretlife-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Like a Virgin</i> was certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">diamond</a> by the Recording Industry Association of America and sold more than 21 million copies worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Madonna entered mainstream films in February 1985, beginning with a brief appearance as a club singer in <i><a href="/wiki/Vision_Quest" title="Vision Quest">Vision Quest</a></i>, a romantic drama film. Its soundtrack contained two new singles, her U.S. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chart-topper" title="Chart-topper">number-one single</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Crazy_for_You_(Madonna_song)" title="Crazy for You (Madonna song)">Crazy for You</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Gambler_(Madonna_song)" title="Gambler (Madonna song)">Gambler</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ach_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-ach-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> She also appeared in the comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Desperately_Seeking_Susan" title="Desperately Seeking Susan">Desperately Seeking Susan</a></i> in March 1985, a film which introduced the song "<a href="/wiki/Into_the_Groove" title="Into the Groove">Into the Groove</a>", her first number one single in the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Although not the lead actress for the film, her profile was such that the movie widely became seen (and marketed) as a Madonna vehicle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AmericanF_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-AmericanF-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The New York Times</i> film critic <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Canby" title="Vincent Canby">Vincent Canby</a> named it one of the ten best films of 1985.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> In February 1984, according to the film director <a href="/wiki/Richard_Attenborough" title="Richard Attenborough">Sir Richard Attenborough</a>, Madonna auditioned at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royale_Theatre" title="Royale Theatre">Royale Theatre</a> on <a href="/wiki/Broadway_(Manhattan)" title="Broadway (Manhattan)">Broadway</a> for a dance role in his movie version of <i><a href="/wiki/A_Chorus_Line_(film)" title="A Chorus Line (film)">A Chorus Line</a></i> using her birth-name of Ciccone, but he rejected her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Beginning in April 1985, Madonna embarked on her first concert tour in North America, <a href="/wiki/The_Virgin_Tour" title="The Virgin Tour">The Virgin Tour</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Beastie_Boys" title="Beastie Boys">Beastie Boys</a> as her opening act. She progressed from playing CBGB and the Mudd Club to playing sporting arenas. At that time she released two more hit singles from the album, "<a href="/wiki/Angel_(Madonna_song)" title="Angel (Madonna song)">Angel</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Dress_You_Up" title="Dress You Up">Dress You Up</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> In July, <i><a href="/wiki/Penthouse_(magazine)" title="Penthouse (magazine)">Penthouse</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Playboy" title="Playboy">Playboy</a></i> magazines published a number of nude photos of Madonna, taken in New York in 1978. She had posed for the photographs as she needed money at the time, and was paid as little as $25 a session.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morton134-135_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morton134-135-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> The publication of the photos caused a media uproar, but Madonna remained "unapologetic and defiant".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-musicobio_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-musicobio-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> The photographs were ultimately sold for up to $100,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morton134-135_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morton134-135-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> She referred to the whole experience at the 1985 outdoor <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a> charity concert saying that she would not take her jacket off because "[the media] might hold it against me ten years from now."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-musicobio_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-musicobio-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1986.E2.80.9391:_True_Blue.2C_Who.27s_That_Girl.2C_Like_a_Prayer.2C_and_Dick_Tracy">1986–91: <i>True Blue</i>, <i>Who's That Girl</i>, <i>Like a Prayer</i>, and <i>Dick Tracy</i></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madonna,_Rotterdam,_26-8-1987.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3162" data-file-width="1958" height="275" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Madonna%2C_Rotterdam%2C_26-8-1987.jpg/170px-Madonna%2C_Rotterdam%2C_26-8-1987.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Madonna%2C_Rotterdam%2C_26-8-1987.jpg/255px-Madonna%2C_Rotterdam%2C_26-8-1987.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Madonna%2C_Rotterdam%2C_26-8-1987.jpg/340px-Madonna%2C_Rotterdam%2C_26-8-1987.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Madonna,_Rotterdam,_26-8-1987.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Madonna performing during the <a href="/wiki/Who%27s_That_Girl_World_Tour" title="Who's That Girl World Tour">Who's That Girl World Tour</a>, 1987</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In June 1986, Madonna released her third studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/True_Blue_(Madonna_album)" title="True Blue (Madonna album)">True Blue</a></i>, which was inspired by and dedicated to Sean Penn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine was generally impressed with the effort, writing that the album "sound[s] as if it comes from the heart".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> It spawned three number-one singles on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100: "<a href="/wiki/Live_to_Tell" title="Live to Tell">Live to Tell</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Papa_Don%27t_Preach" title="Papa Don't Preach">Papa Don't Preach</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Open_Your_Heart_(Madonna_song)" title="Open Your Heart (Madonna song)">Open Your Heart</a>", and two more top-five singles: "<a href="/wiki/True_Blue_(Madonna_song)" title="True Blue (Madonna song)">True Blue</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/La_Isla_Bonita" title="La Isla Bonita">La Isla Bonita</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbsingles_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbsingles-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ach_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-ach-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The album topped the charts in over 28 countries worldwide, an unprecedented achievement at the time and became her best-selling studio album of her career to this date with sales of 25 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> In the same year, Madonna also starred in the critically panned film <i><a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Surprise" title="Shanghai Surprise">Shanghai Surprise</a></i> for which she was awarded the Golden Raspberry Award for "worst actress". She also made her theatrical debut in a production of <a href="/wiki/David_Rabe" title="David Rabe">David Rabe</a>'s <i>Goose and Tom-Tom</i>, both co-starring Penn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> The next year, Madonna was featured in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Who%27s_That_Girl_(1987_film)" title="Who's That Girl (1987 film)">Who's That Girl</a></i>. She contributed four songs to its soundtrack, including the <a href="/wiki/Who%27s_That_Girl_(Madonna_song)" title="Who's That Girl (Madonna song)">title track</a> and "<a href="/wiki/Causing_a_Commotion" title="Causing a Commotion">Causing a Commotion</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbsingles_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-bbsingles-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Madonna embarked on the <a href="/wiki/Who%27s_That_Girl_World_Tour" title="Who's That Girl World Tour">Who's That Girl World Tour</a> in July 1987, which continued until September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-showstealer_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-showstealer-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Voller_1999_29_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Voller_1999_29-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> It broke several attendance records, including over 130,000 audience in a concert near Paris, which remains her biggest concert attendance ever.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Later that year, she released a remix album of past hits, titled <i><a href="/wiki/You_Can_Dance" title="You Can Dance">You Can Dance</a></i>, which reached number 14 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbalbums_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-bbalbums-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> After an annulment in December 1987, Madonna filed for divorce from Penn in January 1989 citing irreconcilable differences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-secretlife_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-secretlife-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"In <i>Like a Prayer</i> I've been dealing with more specific issues that mean a lot to me. They're about an assimilation of experiences I've had in my life and in relationships. They're about my mother, my father and my bonds with my family about the pain of dying, or growing up and letting go. [The album] was a real coming-of-age record for me emotionally..... I had to do a lot of soul-searching and I think it is a reflection of that."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—Madonna talking about the inspiration behind <i>Like a Prayer</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bookalbum_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-bookalbum-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>In January 1989, Madonna signed an endorsement deal with soft-drink manufacturer, <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a>. In one of her Pepsi commercials, she debuted her song "<a href="/wiki/Like_a_Prayer_(song)" title="Like a Prayer (song)">Like a Prayer</a>". The corresponding music video featured many <a href="/wiki/Christian_symbolism" title="Christian symbolism">Catholic symbols</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Stigmata" title="Stigmata">stigmata</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cross_burning" title="Cross burning">cross burning</a>, and a dream about making love to a saint, leading the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Vatican</a> to condemn the video. Religious groups sought to ban the commercial and boycott Pepsi products. Pepsi revoked the commercial and canceled her sponsorship contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-foxbio_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-foxbio-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> The song was included on Madonna's fourth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Like_a_Prayer_(album)" title="Like a Prayer (album)">Like a Prayer</a></i>, which was co-written and co-produced by <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Leonard" title="Patrick Leonard">Patrick Leonard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Bray" title="Stephen Bray">Stephen Bray</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna received positive feedback for the album, with <i>Rolling Stone</i> writing that it was "as close to art as pop music gets".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laprsreview_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-laprsreview-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Like a Prayer</i> peaked at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and sold 15 million copies worldwide, with 4 million copies sold in the U.S. alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbalbums_24-3"><a href="#cite_note-bbalbums-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> Six singles were released from the album, including "Like a Prayer", which reached number one, and "<a href="/wiki/Express_Yourself_(Madonna_song)" title="Express Yourself (Madonna song)">Express Yourself</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Cherish_(Madonna_song)" title="Cherish (Madonna song)">Cherish</a>", both peaking at number two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbsingles_25-3"><a href="#cite_note-bbsingles-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ach_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-ach-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> By the end of the 1980s, Madonna was named as the "Artist of the Decade" by MTV, <i>Billboard</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Musician_(magazine)" title="Musician (magazine)">Musician</a></i> magazine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Madonna starred as Breathless Mahoney in the film <a href="/wiki/Dick_Tracy_(1990_film)" title="Dick Tracy (1990 film)"><i>Dick Tracy</i></a> (1990), with <a href="/wiki/Warren_Beatty" title="Warren Beatty">Warren Beatty</a> playing the title role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> Her performance led to a <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award" title="Saturn Award">Saturn Award</a> nomination for <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Saturn Award for Best Actress">Best Actress</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> To accompany the film, she released the soundtrack album, <i><a href="/wiki/I%27m_Breathless" title="I'm Breathless">I'm Breathless</a></i>, which included songs inspired by the film's 1930s setting. It also featured the US number-one hit "<a href="/wiki/Vogue_(Madonna_song)" title="Vogue (Madonna song)">Vogue</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> and "<a href="/wiki/Sooner_or_Later_(Madonna_song)" title="Sooner or Later (Madonna song)">Sooner or Later</a>", which earned songwriter <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Sondheim" title="Stephen Sondheim">Stephen Sondheim</a> an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Academy Award for Best Original Song</a> in 1991.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> While shooting the film, Madonna began a relationship with Beatty which dissolved by the end of 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> In April 1990, Madonna began her <a href="/wiki/Blond_Ambition_World_Tour" title="Blond Ambition World Tour">Blond Ambition World Tour</a>, which was held until August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Rolling Stone</i> called it an "elaborately choreographed, sexually provocative extravaganza" and proclaimed it "the best tour of 1990".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The tour was met with strong reaction from religious groups for her performance of "Like a Virgin", during which two male dancers caressed her body before she simulated masturbation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-showstealer_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-showstealer-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> In response, Madonna said, "The tour in no way hurts anybody's sentiments. It's for open minds and gets them to see sexuality in a different way. Their own and others".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carrie_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-carrie-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Live!_%E2%80%93_Blond_Ambition_World_Tour_90" title="Live! – Blond Ambition World Tour 90">The Laserdisc release</a> of the tour won Madonna a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> in 1992 for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Long_Form_Music_Video" title="Grammy Award for Best Long Form Music Video">Best Long Form Music Video</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grammy_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-grammy-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Immaculate_Collection" title="The Immaculate Collection">The Immaculate Collection</a></i>, Madonna's first greatest-hits <a href="/wiki/Compilation_album" title="Compilation album">compilation album</a>, was released in November 1990. It included two new songs, "<a href="/wiki/Justify_My_Love" title="Justify My Love">Justify My Love</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Rescue_Me_(Madonna_song)" title="Rescue Me (Madonna song)">Rescue Me</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cross28_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-cross28-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was certified diamond by RIAA and sold over 30 million copies worldwide, becoming the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_albums_worldwide" title="List of best-selling albums worldwide">best-selling</a> compilation album by a solo artist in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-diamond_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-diamond-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> "Justify My Love" reached number one in the U.S. and top ten worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ach_37-3"><a href="#cite_note-ach-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> Its music video featured scenes of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sadomasochism" title="Sadomasochism">sadomasochism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bondage_(sexual)" title="Bondage (sexual)">bondage</a>, same-sex kissing, and brief nudity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rebel_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-rebel-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> The video was deemed too sexually explicit for MTV and was banned from the network.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rebel_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-rebel-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna responded to the banning: "Why is it that people are willing to go and watch a movie about someone getting blown to bits for no reason at all, and nobody wants to see two girls kissing and two men snuggling?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In December 1990, Madonna decided to leave <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lynch" title="Jennifer Lynch">Jennifer Lynch</a>'s film, <i><a href="/wiki/Boxing_Helena" title="Boxing Helena">Boxing Helena</a></i>, which she had previously agreed to star in, without any explanation to the producers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Around this time, Madonna had an eight-month relationship with rapper <a href="/wiki/Vanilla_Ice" title="Vanilla Ice">Vanilla Ice</a>; he ended their relationship because of Madonna's <i><a href="/wiki/Sex_(book)" title="Sex (book)">Sex</a></i> book.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> Her first documentary film <i><a href="/wiki/Madonna:_Truth_or_Dare" title="Madonna: Truth or Dare">Truth or Dare</a></i> (known as <i>In Bed with Madonna</i> outside North America)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> was released in May 1991. The documentary chronicled her Blond Ambition World Tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rolling_Biography_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Biography-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1992.E2.80.9397:_Maverick_Records.2C_Sex.2C_Erotica.2C_Bedtime_Stories.2C_Evita.2C_and_motherhood">1992–97: Maverick Records, <i>Sex</i>, <i>Erotica</i>, <i>Bedtime Stories</i>, <i>Evita</i>, and motherhood</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:InThisLifeUnderGround.jpg"><img alt="Image of a blond female facing her left. She has short blonde hair and is wearing a green bra and purple pants with beads on the waist. She is singing to a microphone, which she holds to her mouth with her left arm." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="321" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/InThisLifeUnderGround.jpg/170px-InThisLifeUnderGround.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/InThisLifeUnderGround.jpg/255px-InThisLifeUnderGround.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e2/InThisLifeUnderGround.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:InThisLifeUnderGround.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Madonna performing during <a href="/wiki/The_Girlie_Show_World_Tour" title="The Girlie Show World Tour">The Girlie Show World Tour</a>, 1993</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1992, Madonna had a role in <i><a href="/wiki/A_League_of_Their_Own" title="A League of Their Own">A League of Their Own</a></i> as Mae Mordabito, a baseball player on an all-women's team. She recorded the film's theme song, "<a href="/wiki/This_Used_to_Be_My_Playground" title="This Used to Be My Playground">This Used to Be My Playground</a>", which became a Hot 100 number one hit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ach_37-4"><a href="#cite_note-ach-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The same year, she founded her own entertainment company, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maverick_(entertainment_company)" title="Maverick (entertainment company)">Maverick</a>, consisting of a record company (<a href="/wiki/Maverick_Records" title="Maverick Records">Maverick Records</a>), a film production company (<a href="/wiki/Maverick_Films" title="Maverick Films">Maverick Films</a>), and associated music publishing, television broadcasting, book publishing and merchandising divisions. The deal was a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Time_Warner" title="Time Warner">Time Warner</a> and paid Madonna an advance of $60 million. It gave her 20% royalties from the music proceedings, one of the highest rates in the industry, equaled at that time only by Michael Jackson's royalty rate established a year earlier with <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_-_.2460_million_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_-_.2460_million-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> The first release from the venture was Madonna's book, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Sex_(book)" title="Sex (book)">Sex</a></i>. It consisted of sexually provocative and explicit images, photographed by <a href="/wiki/Steven_Meisel" title="Steven Meisel">Steven Meisel</a>. The book caused strong negative reaction from the media and the general public, but sold 1.5 million copies at $50 each in a matter of days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SEX_and_Erotica_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-SEX_and_Erotica-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> At the same time she released her fifth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Erotica_(Madonna_album)" title="Erotica (Madonna album)">Erotica</a></i>, which debuted at number two on the <i>Billboard</i> 200.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbalbums_24-4"><a href="#cite_note-bbalbums-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SEX_and_Erotica_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-SEX_and_Erotica-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> Its title track peaked at number three on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ach_37-5"><a href="#cite_note-ach-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Erotica</i> also produced five further singles: "<a href="/wiki/Deeper_and_Deeper" title="Deeper and Deeper">Deeper and Deeper</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Bad_Girl_(Madonna_song)" title="Bad Girl (Madonna song)">Bad Girl</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Fever_(Little_Willie_John_song)" title="Fever (Little Willie John song)">Fever</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Rain_(Madonna_song)" title="Rain (Madonna song)">Rain</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Bye_Bye_Baby_(Madonna_song)" title="Bye Bye Baby (Madonna song)">Bye Bye Baby</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> The provocative imagery continued in the 1990s with the <a href="/wiki/Erotic_thriller" title="Erotic thriller">erotic thriller</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Body_of_Evidence_(1993_film)" title="Body of Evidence (1993 film)">Body of Evidence</a></i>, a film which contained scenes of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sadomasochism" title="Sadomasochism">sadomasochism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bondage_(BDSM)" title="Bondage (BDSM)">bondage</a>. It was poorly received by critics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> She also starred in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Dangerous_Game_(1993_film)" title="Dangerous Game (1993 film)">Dangerous Game</a></i>, which was released straight to video in North America. <i>The New York Times</i> described the film as "angry and painful, and the pain feels real."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In September 1993, Madonna embarked on <a href="/wiki/The_Girlie_Show_World_Tour" title="The Girlie Show World Tour">The Girlie Show World Tour</a>, in which she dressed as a whip-cracking <a href="/wiki/Dominatrix" title="Dominatrix">dominatrix</a> surrounded by topless dancers. The show faced negative reaction, specifically in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> where she rubbed the island's flag between her legs on stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-showstealer_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-showstealer-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> In March 1994, <a href="/wiki/Madonna_on_Late_Show_with_David_Letterman" title="Madonna on Late Show with David Letterman">she appeared as a guest</a> on the <i><a href="/wiki/Late_Show_with_David_Letterman" title="Late Show with David Letterman">Late Show with David Letterman</a></i>, using profanity that was required to be censored on television and handing Letterman a pair of her underwear and asking him to smell it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> The releases of her sexually explicit films, albums and book, and the aggressive appearance on Letterman all made critics question Madonna as a sexual renegade. She faced strong negative publicity from critics and fans, who commented that "she had gone too far" and that her career was over.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Biographer <a href="/wiki/J._Randy_Taraborrelli" title="J. Randy Taraborrelli">J. Randy Taraborrelli</a> described her ballad "<a href="/wiki/I%27ll_Remember" title="I'll Remember">I'll Remember</a>" (1994) as an attempt to tone down her provocative image. The song was recorded for <a href="/wiki/Alek_Keshishian" title="Alek Keshishian">Alek Keshishian</a>'s film <i><a href="/wiki/With_Honors_(film)" title="With Honors (film)">With Honors</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> She made a subdued appearance with Letterman at an awards show and appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_with_Jay_Leno" title="The Tonight Show with Jay Leno">The Tonight Show with Jay Leno</a></i> after realizing that she needed to change her musical direction in order to sustain her popularity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tara235_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-tara235-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> With her sixth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Bedtime_Stories_(Madonna_album)" title="Bedtime Stories (Madonna album)">Bedtime Stories</a></i> (1994), Madonna employed a softer image to try to improve the public perception of her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tara235_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-tara235-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> The album debuted at number three on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and produced four singles, including "<a href="/wiki/Secret_(Madonna_song)" title="Secret (Madonna song)">Secret</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Take_a_Bow_(Madonna_song)" title="Take a Bow (Madonna song)">Take a Bow</a>", the latter topping the Hot 100 for seven weeks, the longest period of any Madonna single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> At the same time, she became romantically involved with fitness trainer Carlos Leon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Something_to_Remember" title="Something to Remember">Something to Remember</a></i>, a collection of ballads, was released in November 1995. The album featured three new songs: "<a href="/wiki/You%27ll_See" title="You'll See">You'll See</a>", "<a href="/wiki/One_More_Chance_(Madonna_song)" title="One More Chance (Madonna song)">One More Chance</a>", and a cover of <a href="/wiki/Marvin_Gaye" title="Marvin Gaye">Marvin Gaye</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_You_(Marvin_Gaye_song)" title="I Want You (Marvin Gaye song)">I Want You</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ach_37-6"><a href="#cite_note-ach-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-str_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-str-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>1996 saw the release of <i><a href="/wiki/Evita_(1996_film)" title="Evita (1996 film)">Evita</a></i>, in which Madonna played the title role of <a href="/wiki/Eva_Per%C3%B3n" title="Eva Perón">Eva Perón</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msn_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-msn-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-evitany_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-evitany-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> For a long time, Madonna had desired to play Perón and even wrote to director <a href="/wiki/Alan_Parker" title="Alan Parker">Alan Parker</a>, explaining how she would be perfect for the part. She stated, "This is the role I was born to play. I put everything of me into this because it was much more than a role in a movie. It was exhilarating and intimidating at the same time..... And I am prouder of Evita than anything else I have done."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> After securing it, she underwent vocal training and learned about the history of Argentina and Perón. During shooting she fell sick many times due to the intense emotional effort required.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> However, as she told Oprah, she was also pregnant during the filming, which was also a factor: "I was winded after every take. I had to lie on the couch every ten minutes so I could recover from dizzy spells, I was worried that I was shaking the baby around too much and that would injure it in some way."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oprah_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oprah-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> Nevertheless, Madonna managed to find a positive side to those problems, which she wrote in her personal diary at the time: "Ironically, this feeling of vulnerability and weakness is helping me in the movie. I'm sure Evita felt this way every day of her life once she discovered she was ill."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After its release, Evita garnered critical appreciation. Zach Conner from <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine commented "It's a relief to say that <i>Evita</i> is pretty damn fine, well cast and handsomely visualized. Madonna once again confounds our expectations. She plays Evita with a poignant weariness and has more than just a bit of star quality. Love or hate Madonna-Eva, she is a magnet for all eyes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna won a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe Award</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actress_%E2%80%93_Motion_Picture_Musical_or_Comedy" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actress – Motion Picture Musical or Comedy">Best Actress in Motion Picture Musical or Comedy</a> for the role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn2008_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn2008-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> She released three singles from the <a href="/wiki/Evita_(soundtrack)" title="Evita (soundtrack)"><i>Evita</i> soundtrack album</a> including "<a href="/wiki/You_Must_Love_Me" title="You Must Love Me">You Must Love Me</a>" (which won an Academy Award for Best Original Song in 1997) and "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Cry_for_Me_Argentina#Madonna_version" title="Don't Cry for Me Argentina">Don't Cry for Me Argentina</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna was later presented with the Artist Achievement Award by <a href="/wiki/Tony_Bennett" title="Tony Bennett">Tony Bennett</a> at the 1996 <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Award" title="Billboard Music Award"><i>Billboard</i> Music Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> On October 14, 1996, Madonna gave birth to Lourdes Maria Ciccone Leon, her daughter with Leon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> Biographer Mary Cross writes that although Madonna was often ill during the filming and worried that her pregnancy would harm the film, she reached some important personal goals: "Now 38 years old, Madonna had at last triumphed on screen and achieved her dream of having a child, both in the same year. She had reached another turning point in her career, reinventing herself and her image with the public."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Her relationship with Carlos Leon ended in May 1997;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> she declared that they were "better off as best friends."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> After Lourdes' birth, Madonna became involved in Eastern mysticism and <a href="/wiki/Kabbalah" title="Kabbalah">Kabbalah</a>. She was introduced to Jewish mysticism by actress <a href="/wiki/Sandra_Bernhard" title="Sandra Bernhard">Sandra Bernhard</a> in 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1998.E2.80.932002:_Ray_of_Light.2C_Music.2C_and_second_marriage">1998–2002: <i>Ray of Light</i>, <i>Music</i>, and second marriage</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MadonnaDrownedWorld8_cropped.jpg"><img alt="A blond woman sitting on a block of hay. She is playing a guitar and singing in front of a standing microphone. She has short hair and wears grey colored cowboy clothes." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="368" data-file-width="240" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/MadonnaDrownedWorld8_cropped.jpg/170px-MadonnaDrownedWorld8_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4c/MadonnaDrownedWorld8_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4c/MadonnaDrownedWorld8_cropped.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MadonnaDrownedWorld8_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Madonna performing on the <a href="/wiki/Drowned_World_Tour" title="Drowned World Tour">Drowned World Tour</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Madonna's seventh studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Ray_of_Light" title="Ray of Light">Ray of Light</a></i>, (1998) reflected a change in her perception and image.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> She collaborated with electronica producer <a href="/wiki/William_Orbit" title="William Orbit">William Orbit</a> and wanted to create a sound that could blend dance music with pop and British rock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wync_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-wync-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> American music critic <a href="/wiki/Ann_Powers" title="Ann Powers">Ann Powers</a> explained that what Madonna searched for with Orbit "was a kind of a lushness that she wanted for this record. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Techno_music" title="Techno music">Techno</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rave_music" title="Rave music">rave</a> was happening in the 90's and had a lot of different forms. There was very experimental, more hard stuff like Aphex Twin. There was party stuff like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fatboy_Slim" title="Fatboy Slim">Fatboy Slim</a>. That's not what Madonna wanted for this. She wanted something more like a singer-songwriter, really. And William Orbit provided her with that."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wync_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-wync-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> The album garnered critical acclaim and <a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a> declared it as "one of the great pop masterpieces of the '90s".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Ray of Light</i> was honored with four <a href="/wiki/41st_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="41st Annual Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> listed it among "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_500_Greatest_Albums_of_All_Time" title="The 500 Greatest Albums of All Time">The 500 Greatest Albums of All Time</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-madonnasecret_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-madonnasecret-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> Commercially, the album peaked at number one in numerous countries and sold more than 16 million copies worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> The album's first single, "<a href="/wiki/Frozen_(Madonna_song)" title="Frozen (Madonna song)">Frozen</a>", became Madonna's first single to debut at number one in the UK, while in the U.S. it became her sixth number-two single and set another record for Madonna as the artist with the most number two hits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ach_37-7"><a href="#cite_note-ach-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> The second single, "<a href="/wiki/Ray_of_Light_(song)" title="Ray of Light (song)">Ray of Light</a>", debuted at number five on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The 1998 edition of <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness Book of World Records</a></i> stated: "No female artist has sold more records than Madonna around the world".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1999, Madonna signed to play a violin teacher in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Heart" title="Music of the Heart">Music of the Heart</a></i> but left the project, citing "creative differences" with director <a href="/wiki/Wes_Craven" title="Wes Craven">Wes Craven</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNRev_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNNRev-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> She recorded the single "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_Stranger" title="Beautiful Stranger">Beautiful Stranger</a>" for the 1999 film <i><a href="/wiki/Austin_Powers:_The_Spy_Who_Shagged_Me" title="Austin Powers: The Spy Who Shagged Me">Austin Powers: The Spy Who Shagged Me</a></i>. It reached number 19 on the Hot 100 solely on radio airplay and earned Madonna a Grammy Award for "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Song_Written_for_a_Motion_Picture,_Television_or_Other_Visual_Media" title="Grammy Award for Best Song Written for a Motion Picture, Television or Other Visual Media">Best Song Written for a Motion Picture, Television or Other Visual Media</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ach_37-8"><a href="#cite_note-ach-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grammy_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-grammy-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2000, Madonna starred in the film, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Next_Best_Thing" title="The Next Best Thing">The Next Best Thing</a></i>, and contributed two songs to the film's soundtrack; "Time Stood Still" and a cover of <a href="/wiki/Don_McLean" title="Don McLean">Don McLean</a>'s 1971 song "<a href="/wiki/American_Pie_(song)" title="American Pie (song)">American Pie</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> She released her eighth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Music_(Madonna_album)" title="Music (Madonna album)">Music</a></i>, in September 2000. It featured elements from the <a href="/wiki/Electronic_dance_music" title="Electronic dance music">electronica</a>-inspired <i>Ray of Light</i> era, and catered to her gay audience. Collaborating with French producer <a href="/wiki/Mirwais_Ahmadza%C3%AF" title="Mirwais Ahmadzaï">Mirwais Ahmadzaï</a>, Madonna commented: "I love to work with the weirdos that no one knows about—the people who have raw talent and who are making music unlike anyone else out there. <i>Music</i> is the future of sound."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bronmusic_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-bronmusic-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">Stephen Thomas Erlewine</a> from <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> felt that "<i>Music</i> blows by in a kaleidoscopic rush of color, technique, style and substance. It has so many depth and layers that it's easily as self-aware and earnest as <i>Ray of Light</i>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> The album took the number-one position in more than 20 countries worldwide and sold four million copies in the first ten days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-madonnasecret_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-madonnasecret-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> In the U.S., <i>Music</i> debuted at the top, and became her first number-one album in eleven years since <i>Like a Prayer</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> It produced three singles: the Hot 100 number one "<a href="/wiki/Music_(Madonna_song)" title="Music (Madonna song)">Music</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Tell_Me_(Madonna_song)" title="Don't Tell Me (Madonna song)">Don't Tell Me</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/What_It_Feels_Like_for_a_Girl" title="What It Feels Like for a Girl">What It Feels Like for a Girl</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ach_37-9"><a href="#cite_note-ach-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The music video of "What It Feels Like for a Girl" depicted Madonna committing acts of crime and vandalism, and was banned by MTV and <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>She met director <a href="/wiki/Guy_Ritchie" title="Guy Ritchie">Guy Ritchie</a>, who would become her second husband, in November 1998 and gave birth to their son Rocco John Ritchie on August 11, 2000 in Los Angeles. Rocco and Madonna suffered complications from the birth due to her experiencing <a href="/wiki/Placenta_praevia" title="Placenta praevia">placenta praevia</a>. He was christened at <a href="/wiki/Dornoch_Cathedral" title="Dornoch Cathedral">Dornoch Cathedral</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dornoch" title="Dornoch">Dornoch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, on December 21, 2000. Madonna married Ritchie the following day at nearby <a href="/wiki/Skibo_Castle" title="Skibo Castle">Skibo Castle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> Her fifth concert tour, titled <a href="/wiki/Drowned_World_Tour" title="Drowned World Tour">Drowned World Tour</a>, started in April 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-showstealer_50-3"><a href="#cite_note-showstealer-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> The tour visited cities in the U.S. and Europe and was the highest-grossing concert tour of the year by a solo artist, earning $75 million from 47 sold-out shows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> She also released her second greatest-hits collection, titled <i><a href="/wiki/GHV2" title="GHV2">GHV2</a></i>, to coincide with the <a href="/wiki/Drowned_World_Tour_2001" title="Drowned World Tour 2001">home video release of the tour</a>. <i>GHV2</i> debuted at number seven on the <i>Billboard</i> 200.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusicghv2_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicghv2-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Madonna starred in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Swept_Away_(2002_film)" title="Swept Away (2002 film)">Swept Away</a></i>, directed by Ritchie. Released <a href="/wiki/Direct-to-video" title="Direct-to-video">direct-to-video</a> in the UK, the film was a commercial and critical failure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> In May 2002 she appeared in London in the West End play <i><a href="/wiki/Up_for_Grabs_(play)" title="Up for Grabs (play)">Up For Grabs</a></i> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wyndhams_Theatre" title="Wyndhams Theatre">Wyndhams Theatre</a> (billed as 'Madonna Ritchie'), to universally bad reviews and was described as "the evening's biggest disappointment" by one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> That October, she released "<a href="/wiki/Die_Another_Day_(song)" title="Die Another Day (song)">Die Another Day</a>", the title song of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Bond_(film_series)" title="James Bond (film series)">James Bond</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Another_Day" title="Die Another Day">Die Another Day</a></i>, in which she had a <a href="/wiki/Cameo_appearance" title="Cameo appearance">cameo role</a>, described by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> film reviewer as "incredibly wooden".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> The song reached number eight on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 and was nominated for both a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe Award</a> for Best Original Song and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Raspberry_Award" title="Golden Raspberry Award">Golden Raspberry</a> for Worst Song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ach_37-10"><a href="#cite_note-ach-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2003.E2.80.9306:_American_Life.2C_children.27s_books.2C_and_Confessions_on_a_Dance_Floor">2003–06: <i>American Life</i>, children's books, and <i>Confessions on a Dance Floor</i></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IsaacFresno2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2288" data-file-width="1712" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/IsaacFresno2.jpg/170px-IsaacFresno2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/IsaacFresno2.jpg/255px-IsaacFresno2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/IsaacFresno2.jpg/340px-IsaacFresno2.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IsaacFresno2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Madonna performing during <a href="/wiki/Confessions_Tour" title="Confessions Tour">Confessions Tour</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following <i>Die Another Day</i>, Madonna collaborated with fashion photographer <a href="/wiki/Steven_Klein_(photographer)" title="Steven Klein (photographer)">Steven Klein</a> in 2003 for an exhibition installation named <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/X-STaTIC_Pro%3DCeSS" title="X-STaTIC Pro=CeSS">X-STaTIC Pro=CeSS</a></i>. It included photography from a photo shoot in <i><a href="/wiki/W_(magazine)" title="W (magazine)">W</a></i> magazine, and seven video segments. The installation ran from March to May in New York's <a href="/wiki/Deitch_Projects" title="Deitch Projects">Deitch Projects</a> gallery. It then traveled the world in an edited form.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> The same year, Madonna released her ninth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/American_Life" title="American Life">American Life</a></i>, which was based on her observations of American society, and received mixed reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> She commented, "[<i>American Life</i>] was like a trip down memory lane, looking back at everything I've accomplished and all the things I once valued and all the things that were important to me."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvamerican_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtvamerican-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> Larry Flick from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Advocate" title="The Advocate">The Advocate</a></i> felt that "<i>American Life</i> is an album that is among her most adventurous and lyrically intelligent" while condemning it as "a lazy, half-arsed effort to sound and take her seriously."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvamerican_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-mtvamerican-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/American_Life_(song)" title="American Life (song)">title song</a> peaked at number 37 on the Hot 100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ach_37-11"><a href="#cite_note-ach-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> Its original music video was canceled as Madonna thought that the video, featuring violence and war imagery, would be deemed unpatriotic since America was then at <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">war with Iraq</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> With only four million copies sold worldwide, <i>American Life</i> was the lowest-selling album of her career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
