<p>Madonna gave another provocative performance later that year at the <a href="/wiki/2003_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2003 MTV Video Music Awards">2003 MTV Video Music Awards</a>, while singing "<a href="/wiki/Hollywood_(Madonna_song)" title="Hollywood (Madonna song)">Hollywood</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a>. Madonna sparked controversy for kissing Spears and Aguilera suggestively during the performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> In October 2003, Madonna provided guest vocals on Spears' single "<a href="/wiki/Me_Against_the_Music" title="Me Against the Music">Me Against the Music</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> It was followed with the release of <i><a href="/wiki/Remixed_%26_Revisited" title="Remixed &amp; Revisited">Remixed &amp; Revisited</a></i>. The EP contained remixed versions of songs from <i>American Life</i> and included "Your Honesty", a previously unreleased track from the <i>Bedtime Stories</i> recording sessions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna also signed a contract with <a href="/wiki/Callaway_Arts_%26_Entertainment" title="Callaway Arts &amp; Entertainment">Callaway Arts &amp; Entertainment</a> to be the author of five children's books. The first of these books, titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_English_Roses" title="The English Roses">The English Roses</a></i>, was published in September 2003. The story was about four English schoolgirls and their envy and jealousy of each other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> Kate Kellway from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> commented, "[Madonna] is an actress playing at what she can never be—a <a href="/wiki/J._K._Rowling" title="J. K. Rowling">JK Rowling</a>, an English rose."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> The book debuted at the top of <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times_Best_Seller_list" title="The New York Times Best Seller list"><i>The New York Times</i> Best Seller list</a> and became the fastest-selling children's picture book of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-womenworld_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-womenworld-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The next year, Madonna and Maverick sued <a href="/wiki/Warner_Music_Group" title="Warner Music Group">Warner Music Group</a> and its former parent company <a href="/wiki/Time_Warner" title="Time Warner">Time Warner</a>, claiming that mismanagement of resources and poor bookkeeping had cost the company millions of dollars. In return, Warner filed a countersuit alleging that Maverick had lost tens of millions of dollars on its own.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-labelsuit_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-labelsuit-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> The dispute was resolved when the Maverick shares, owned by Madonna and Ronnie Dashev, were purchased by Warner. Madonna and Dashev's company became a wholly owned subsidiary of Warner Music, but Madonna was still signed to Warner under a separate recording contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-labelsuit_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-labelsuit-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In mid-2004, Madonna embarked on the <a href="/wiki/Re-Invention_World_Tour" title="Re-Invention World Tour">Re-Invention World Tour</a> in the U.S., Canada, and Europe. It became the highest-grossing tour of 2004, earning around $120 million and became the subject of her documentary <i><a href="/wiki/I%27m_Going_to_Tell_You_a_Secret" title="I'm Going to Tell You a Secret">I'm Going to Tell You a Secret</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2004, she was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/UK_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="UK Music Hall of Fame">UK Music Hall of Fame</a> as one of its five founding members, along with <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Marley" title="Bob Marley">Bob Marley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> In January 2005, Madonna performed a cover version of the <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a> song "<a href="/wiki/Imagine_(John_Lennon_song)" title="Imagine (John Lennon song)">Imagine</a>" at <a href="/wiki/Tsunami_Aid" title="Tsunami Aid">Tsunami Aid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> She also performed at the <a href="/wiki/Live_8" title="Live 8">Live 8</a> benefit concert in London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:25em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"I tried several different things when Stuart [producer Stuart Price] brought me music. And it was like divine inspiration. It just clicked, like: 'This is the direction of my record.' That's what we intended, to make a record that you can play at a party or in your car, where you don't have to skip past a ballad. It's nonstop."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—Madonna talking about <i>Confessions on a Dance Floor</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>Her tenth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Confessions_on_a_Dance_Floor" title="Confessions on a Dance Floor">Confessions on a Dance Floor</a></i>, was released in November 2005. Musically the album was structured like a club set composed by a DJ with Keith Caulfield from <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> commented that the album was a "welcome return to form for the Queen of Pop."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbalbum_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbalbum-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> The album won a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/49th_Grammy_Awards" title="49th Grammy Awards">Grammy Award</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Electronic/Dance_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Electronic/Dance Album">Best Electronic/Dance Album</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grammy_73-2"><a href="#cite_note-grammy-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Confessions on a Dance Floor</i> and its lead single, "<a href="/wiki/Hung_Up" title="Hung Up">Hung Up</a>", went on to reach number one in 40 and 41 countries respectively, earning a place in <i>Guinness World Records</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guinness_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-guinness-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> The song contained a sample of <a href="/wiki/ABBA" title="ABBA">ABBA</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Gimme!_Gimme!_Gimme!_(A_Man_After_Midnight)" title="Gimme! Gimme! Gimme! (A Man After Midnight)">Gimme! Gimme! Gimme! (A Man After Midnight)</a>", only the second time that ABBA has allowed their work to be used. ABBA songwriter <a href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B6rn_Ulvaeus" title="Björn Ulvaeus">Björn Ulvaeus</a> remarked "It is a wonderful track—100 per cent solid pop music."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Sorry_(Madonna_song)" title="Sorry (Madonna song)">Sorry</a>", the second single, became Madonna's twelfth number-one single in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Madonna embarked on the <a href="/wiki/Confessions_Tour" title="Confessions Tour">Confessions Tour</a> in May 2006, which had a global audience of 1.2 million and grossed over $193.7 million, becoming the highest-grossing tour to that date for a female artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna used religious symbols, such as the <a href="/wiki/Crucifix" title="Crucifix">crucifix</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crown_of_Thorns" title="Crown of Thorns">Crown of Thorns</a>, in the performance of "Live to Tell". It caused the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Jewish_Communities_of_Russia" title="Federation of Jewish Communities of Russia">Federation of Jewish Communities of Russia</a> to urge all their members to boycott her concert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> At the same time, the <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_the_Phonographic_Industry" title="International Federation of the Phonographic Industry">International Federation of the Phonographic Industry</a> (IFPI) announced officially that Madonna had sold over 200 million copies for her albums alone worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IFPI_2006_Report_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-IFPI_2006_Report-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>While on tour, Madonna participated in the <a href="/wiki/Raising_Malawi" title="Raising Malawi">Raising Malawi</a> initiative by partially funding an orphanage in and traveling to that country. While there, she decided to adopt a boy named David Banda in October 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> The adoption raised strong public reaction, because Malawian law requires would-be parents to reside in Malawi for one year before adopting, which Madonna did not do.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> She addressed this on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Oprah_Winfrey_Show" title="The Oprah Winfrey Show">The Oprah Winfrey Show</a></i>, saying that there were no written adoption laws in Malawi that regulated foreign adoption. She described how Banda had been suffering from <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a> after surviving <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> when she first met him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup> Banda's biological father, Yohane, commented, "These so-called human rights activists are harassing me every day, threatening me that I am not aware of what I am doing..... They want me to support their court case, a thing I cannot do for I know what I agreed with Madonna and her husband." The adoption was finalized in May 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A clothing line titled <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fashion_brands_by_Madonna#M_by_Madonna" title="Fashion brands by Madonna">M by Madonna</a></i>, in collaboration with Swedish clothing retailer <a href="/wiki/H%26M" title="H&amp;M">H&amp;M</a>, was launched internationally in 2006. The collection consisted of leather trench coats, sequined shift dresses, cream-colored calf-length pants, and matching cropped jackets. H&amp;M said the collection reflected Madonna's "timeless, unique and always glamorous style."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2007.E2.80.9309:_Live_Nation_and_Hard_Candy">2007–09: Live Nation and <i>Hard Candy</i></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nathan_Rissman_and_Madonna_by_David_Shankbone.jpg"><img alt="Picture of a blond young man wearing a black suit with a black jacket. Next to him is a blond middle-aged female wearing an orange dress. They're both smiling towards the camera." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Nathan_Rissman_and_Madonna_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/220px-Nathan_Rissman_and_Madonna_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Nathan_Rissman_and_Madonna_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/330px-Nathan_Rissman_and_Madonna_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Nathan_Rissman_and_Madonna_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/440px-Nathan_Rissman_and_Madonna_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nathan_Rissman_and_Madonna_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Madonna and Nathan Rissman at the premiere of <i><a href="/wiki/I_Am_Because_We_Are" title="I Am Because We Are">I Am Because We Are</a></i> at the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Tribeca_Film_Festival" title="Tribeca Film Festival">Tribeca Film Festival</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Madonna released the song "<a href="/wiki/Hey_You_(Madonna_song)" title="Hey You (Madonna song)">Hey You</a>" for the <a href="/wiki/Live_Earth" title="Live Earth">Live Earth</a> series of concerts. The song was available as a free download during its first week of release. She also performed it at the <a href="/wiki/Live_Earth_concert,_London" title="Live Earth concert, London">London Live Earth concert</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna announced her departure from Warner Bros. Records, and a new $120 million, ten-year <a href="/wiki/360_deal" title="360 deal">360 deal</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Live_Nation" title="Live Nation">Live Nation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> She produced and wrote <i><a href="/wiki/I_Am_Because_We_Are" title="I Am Because We Are">I Am Because We Are</a></i>, a documentary on the problems faced by Malawians. The documentary was directed by Nathan Rissman, who worked as Madonna's gardener.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iabwa_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-iabwa-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup> She also directed her first film <i><a href="/wiki/Filth_and_Wisdom" title="Filth and Wisdom">Filth and Wisdom</a></i>. The plot of the film revolved around three friends and their aspirations. <i>The Times</i> said she had "done herself proud" while <i>The Daily Telegraph</i> described the film as "not an entirely unpromising first effort [but] Madonna would do well to hang on to her day job."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> announced Madonna as one of the five inductees of 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup> At the induction ceremony on March 10, 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rsinducted_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-rsinducted-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna did not sing but asked fellow Hall of Fame inductees and Michigan natives <a href="/wiki/The_Stooges" title="The Stooges">The Stooges</a> to perform her songs "Burning Up" and "Ray of Light". She thanked Christopher Flynn, her dance teacher from 35 years earlier, for his encouragement to follow her dreams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Madonna released her eleventh studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Hard_Candy_(Madonna_album)" title="Hard Candy (Madonna album)">Hard Candy</a></i>, in April 2008. Containing R&amp;B and <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">urban pop</a> influences, the songs on <i>Hard Candy</i> were autobiographical in nature and saw Madonna collaborating with <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a> and <a href="/wiki/Danja_(record_producer)" title="Danja (record producer)">Nate "Danja" Hills</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timbalandhot_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-timbalandhot-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> The album debuted at number one in thirty seven countries and on the <i>Billboard</i> 200.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup> Don Shewey from <i>Rolling Stone</i> complimented it as an "impressive taste of her upcoming tour."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> It received generally positive reviews worldwide though some critics panned it as "an attempt to harness the urban market".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:25em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"Probably in many respects most of the songs [on <i>Hard Candy</i>] are [autobiographical]. But in more of an unconscious way. I don't really think about telling personal stories when I'm writing music. It just comes. And then a lot of times, six months later, eight months later, I go, 'Oh, that's what I wrote that song about.' But that's when I play the song for lots of people and they all go, 'Oh, I can totally relate to that.'"</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">— Madonna talking about the inspiration behind <i>Hard Candy</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sischy2008_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sischy2008-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/4_Minutes_(Madonna_song)" title="4 Minutes (Madonna song)">4 Minutes</a>" was released as the album's lead single and peaked at number three on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100. It was Madonna's 37th top-ten hit on the chart—it pushed Madonna past <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a> as the artist with the most top-ten hits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mariahmadonna_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-mariahmadonna-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> In the UK, she retained her record for the most number-one singles for a female artist; "4 Minutes" becoming her thirteenth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> At the 23rd <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japan_Gold_Disc_Awards" title="Japan Gold Disc Awards">Japan Gold Disc Awards</a>, Madonna received her fifth Artist of the Year trophy from <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_Japan" title="Recording Industry Association of Japan">Recording Industry Association of Japan</a>, the most for any artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> To further promote the album, Madonna embarked on the <a href="/wiki/Sticky_%26_Sweet_Tour" title="Sticky &amp; Sweet Tour">Sticky &amp; Sweet Tour</a>; her first major venture with Live Nation. With a gross of $280 million, it became the highest-grossing tour by a solo artist then, surpassing the previous record Madonna set with the Confessions Tour; it was later surpassed by <a href="/wiki/Roger_Waters" title="Roger Waters">Roger Waters</a>' <a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Live_(concert_tour)" title="The Wall Live (concert tour)">The Wall Live</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sticky_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-sticky-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Wall_Live_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Wall_Live-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup> It was extended to the next year, adding new European dates, and after it ended, the total gross was $408 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sticky_190-1"><a href="#cite_note-sticky-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Life with My Sister Madonna</i>, a book by Madonna's brother Christopher, debuted at number two on <i>The New York Times</i> bestseller list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytb_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytb-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup> The book caused some friction between Madonna and her brother, because of the unsolicited publication.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup> Problems also arose between Madonna and Ritchie, with the media reporting that they were on the verge of separation. Ultimately, Madonna filed for divorce from Ritchie, citing irreconcilable differences, which was finalized in December 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup> She decided to adopt from Malawi. The country's High Court initially approved the adoption of Chifundo "Mercy" James; however, the application was rejected because Madonna was not a resident of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mercyjames_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-mercyjames-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna appealed, and on June 12, 2009, the Supreme Court of Malawi granted Madonna the right to adopt Mercy James.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> She also released <i><a href="/wiki/Celebration_(Madonna_album)" title="Celebration (Madonna album)">Celebration</a></i>, her third greatest-hits album and final release with Warner. It contained the new songs "<a href="/wiki/Celebration_(Madonna_song)" title="Celebration (Madonna song)">Celebration</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Revolver_(song)" title="Revolver (song)">Revolver</a>" along with 34 hits spanning her career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celebraterelease_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-celebraterelease-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Celebration</i> reached number one in the UK, tying her with Elvis Presley as the solo act with most number one albums in the British chart history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbmadge_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbmadge-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup> She appeared at the <a href="/wiki/2009_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2009 MTV Video Music Awards">2009 MTV Video Music Awards</a> on September 13, 2009, to speak in tribute to deceased pop star <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Controversy erupted when Madonna decided to adopt from Malawi again. Chifundo "Mercy" James was finally adopted on June 2009. Madonna had known Mercy from the time she went to adopt David. Mercy's grandmother had initially protested the adoption, but later gave in, saying "At first I didn't want her to go but as a family we had to sit down and reach an agreement and we agreed that Mercy should go. The men insisted that Mercy be adopted and I won't resist anymore. I still love Mercy. She is my dearest." Mercy's father was still adamant saying that he could not support the adoption since he was alive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Madonna ended the 2000s as the best-selling single artist of the decade in the U.S. and the most-played artist of the decade in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Billboard</i> also announced her as the third top-touring artist of the decade—behind only <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a> and <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a>—with a gross of over $801 million, 6.3 million attendance and 244 sell-outs of 248 shows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010.E2.80.9312:_W.E..2C_MDNA.2C_and_business_ventures">2010–12: <i>W.E.</i>, <i>MDNA</i>, and business ventures</span></h3>
<p>Madonna performed at the <a href="/wiki/Hope_for_Haiti_Now:_A_Global_Benefit_for_Earthquake_Relief" title="Hope for Haiti Now: A Global Benefit for Earthquake Relief">Hope for Haiti Now: A Global Benefit for Earthquake Relief</a> concert in January 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup> In April she released her third live album, <i><a href="/wiki/Sticky_%26_Sweet_Tour_(album)" title="Sticky &amp; Sweet Tour (album)">Sticky &amp; Sweet Tour</a></i>. It was her first release under Live Nation, but was distributed by Warner Bros.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna granted American TV show <i><a href="/wiki/Glee_(TV_series)" title="Glee (TV series)">Glee</a></i> the rights to her entire catalogue of music, and the producers planned an episode featuring Madonna songs exclusively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EW_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-EW-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Glee:_The_Music,_The_Power_of_Madonna" title="Glee: The Music, The Power of Madonna">Glee: The Music, The Power of Madonna</a></i>, an EP containing eight cover versions of Madonna songs featured in the episode, was released afterward and debuted at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madonna_%C3%A0_Nice_17_edit.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1580" data-file-width="1185" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Madonna_%C3%A0_Nice_17_edit.jpg/170px-Madonna_%C3%A0_Nice_17_edit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Madonna_%C3%A0_Nice_17_edit.jpg/255px-Madonna_%C3%A0_Nice_17_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Madonna_%C3%A0_Nice_17_edit.jpg/340px-Madonna_%C3%A0_Nice_17_edit.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Madonna_%C3%A0_Nice_17_edit.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Madonna performing during <a href="/wiki/The_MDNA_Tour" title="The MDNA Tour">The MDNA Tour</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Madonna released the <a href="/wiki/Madonna_fashion_brands" title="Madonna fashion brands">Material Girl</a> clothing line, which she designed with her daughter, Lourdes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mgclothing_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-mgclothing-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> The 1980s inspired clothing line, borrowed from Madonna's punk-girl style when she rose to fame in the 1980s, was released under the <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy's">Macy's</a> label. Madonna also opened a series of <a href="/wiki/Health_club" title="Health club">fitness centers</a> around the world named <a href="/wiki/Hard_Candy_Fitness" title="Hard Candy Fitness">Hard Candy Fitness</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2011, Madonna and MG Icon announced the release of a second fashion brand called <a href="/wiki/Truth_or_Dare_by_Madonna" title="Truth or Dare by Madonna">Truth or Dare by Madonna</a> to include footwear, underclothing, and accessories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> She also directed her second feature film, <i><a href="/wiki/W.E." title="W.E.">W.E.</a></i>, a biographic about the affair between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edward_VIII_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Edward VIII of the United Kingdom">King Edward VIII</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wallis,_Duchess_of_Windsor" title="Wallis, Duchess of Windsor">Wallis Simpson</a>; it was co-written with <a href="/wiki/Alek_Keshishian" title="Alek Keshishian">Alek Keshishian</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup> Critical and commercial response to the film was negative.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna contributed the ballad "<a href="/wiki/Masterpiece_(Madonna_song)" title="Masterpiece (Madonna song)">Masterpiece</a>" for the film's soundtrack, which won her a Golden Globe Award for Best Original Song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, Madonna performed at <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVI_halftime_show" title="Super Bowl XLVI halftime show">Super Bowl XLVI halftime show</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nfl12_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-nfl12-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup> visualized by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cirque_Du_Soleil" title="Cirque Du Soleil">Cirque Du Soleil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jamie_King" title="Jamie King">Jamie King</a> and featured special guests <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LMFAO_(band)" title="LMFAO (band)">LMFAO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M.I.A._(artist)" title="M.I.A. (artist)">M.I.A.</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cee_Lo_Green" title="Cee Lo Green">Cee Lo Green</a>. It became the most-watched Super Bowl halftime show in history with 114 million viewers, higher than the game itself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup> It was also revealed that the singer had signed a three-album deal with <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>, who would act as the distributor in partnership with her <a href="/wiki/360_deal" title="360 deal">360 deal</a> with Live Nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InterscopeDeal_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-InterscopeDeal-219"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup> Her twelfth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/MDNA_(album)" title="MDNA (album)">MDNA</a></i>, was released in March 2012 and saw collaboration with various producers, most notably with William Orbit again and <a href="/wiki/Martin_Solveig" title="Martin Solveig">Martin Solveig</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was well received by music critics,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> with Priya Elan from <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> calling it "a ridiculously enjoyable romp", citing its "psychotic, soul-bearing stuff" as "some of the most visceral stuff she's ever done."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>MDNA</i> debuted at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and many other countries worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna surpassed Elvis Presley's record for the most number-one album by a solo artist in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> The lead single "<a href="/wiki/Give_Me_All_Your_Luvin%27" title="Give Me All Your Luvin'">Give Me All Your Luvin'</a>", featuring guest vocals from Minaj and M.I.A., became Madonna's record-extending 38th top-ten hit on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/The_MDNA_Tour" title="The MDNA Tour">The MDNA Tour</a>, which further promoted the album, began in May 2012 in <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a>, Israel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> The tour has received positive critical reception,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup> but featured controversial subjects such as violence, firearms, human rights, nudity and politics. Lawsuits threatened against Madonna have also been engaged from the tour. It was a box office success with a gross of $305.2 million from 88 sold-out shows, and ended as the highest-grossing tour of 2012 and the tenth highest-grossing tour of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mdna_boxscore_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-mdna_boxscore-229"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2013_Billboard_Music_Awards" title="2013 Billboard Music Awards">2013 <i>Billboard</i> Music Awards</a>, Madonna won three trophies for Top Touring Artist, Top Dance Artist and Top Dance Album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230"><span>[</span>230<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna was named the top-earning celebrity of the year by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a>,</i> earning an estimated $125 million, due to the success of the tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>By 2013, Madonna's <a href="/wiki/Raising_Malawi" title="Raising Malawi">Raising Malawi</a> organization built ten schools to educate 4,000 children in Malawi at a value of $400,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup> When Madonna visited the schools in April 2013, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Malawi" title="President of Malawi">President of Malawi</a> <a href="/wiki/Joyce_Banda" title="Joyce Banda">Joyce Banda</a> expressed criticism of the star and her charity, accusing her of exaggerating her charity's contribution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233"><span>[</span>233<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna responded by releasing a statement saying she was saddened that Banda had chosen to act negatively about her endeavors. "I have no intention of being distracted by these ridiculous allegations," she added. Later, it was confirmed that Banda had not approved the statement released written by her press team and was "incandescent with anger" over the mix-up.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234"><span>[</span>234<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013.E2.80.93present:_secretprojectrevolution_and_Rebel_Heart">2013–present: <i>secretprojectrevolution</i> and <i>Rebel Heart</i></span></h3>
<p>Working with photographer Steven Klein, Madonna completed a 17-minute film called <i><a href="/wiki/Secretprojectrevolution" title="Secretprojectrevolution">secretprojectrevolution</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/BitTorrent_(company)" title="BitTorrent (company)">BitTorrent</a> company was selected by Madonna to release the film as part of a Madonna Bundle. It was released on September 24, 2013, and consisted of the 17-minute film, its stills, a Vice interview and a message from Madonna.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hive_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hive-236"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup> With the film she launched the Art for Freedom initiative, which helped to promote "art and free speech as a means to address persecution and injustice across the globe". The website for the project has had over 3,000 art related submissions since its inception, with Madonna regularly monitoring and enlisting the help of other artists like <a href="/wiki/David_Blaine" title="David Blaine">David Blaine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a> as guest curator.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237"><span>[</span>237<span>]</span></a></sup> After visiting her hometown Detroit during May 2014, Madonna decided to contribute funds to three of the city's organizations, who help in <a href="/wiki/Detroit_bankruptcy" title="Detroit bankruptcy">eliminating poverty</a> from there. The singer released a statement saying that she was inspired by their work, adding that "it was obvious to me that I had to get involved and be part of the solution to help Detroit recover".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>From the beginning of 2014, Madonna started making multiple media appearances. She appeared at the <a href="/wiki/56th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="56th Annual Grammy Awards">56th Annual Grammy Awards</a> in January 2014, performing "Open Your Heart" alongside rappers <a href="/wiki/Macklemore_%26_Ryan_Lewis" title="Macklemore &amp; Ryan Lewis">Macklemore &amp; Ryan Lewis</a> and singer <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lambert_(singer)" title="Mary Lambert (singer)">Mary Lambert</a> who sang their single "<a href="/wiki/Same_Love" title="Same Love">Same Love</a>", as 33 couples were wed onstage, officiated by <a href="/wiki/Queen_Latifah" title="Queen Latifah">Queen Latifah</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239"><span>[</span>239<span>]</span></a></sup> A few days later, she joined singer <a href="/wiki/Miley_Cyrus" title="Miley Cyrus">Miley Cyrus</a> on her <i><a href="/wiki/MTV_Unplugged" title="MTV Unplugged">MTV Unplugged</a></i> special, singing a mash-up of "Don't Tell Me" and Cyrus' single "<a href="/wiki/We_Can%27t_Stop" title="We Can't Stop">We Can't Stop</a>" (2013).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240"><span>[</span>240<span>]</span></a></sup> She also extended her business ventures and in February 2014 the singer premiered MDNA Skin, a range of skin care products, in Tokyo, Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skin_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-skin-241"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup> She also started working on her thirteenth studio album with collaborators including <a href="/wiki/Avicii" title="Avicii">Avicii</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diplo_(producer)" title="Diplo (producer)">Diplo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natalia_Kills" title="Natalia Kills">Natalia Kills</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242"><span>[</span>242<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243"><span>[</span>243<span>]</span></a></sup> In December, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> reported that Madonna had been cast as the face of <a href="/wiki/Versace" title="Versace">Versace</a> for their Spring/Summer 2015 campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244"><span>[</span>244<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 2014, thirteen <a href="/wiki/Demo_(music)" title="Demo (music)">demos</a> of songs from the album leaked onto the Internet. She posted in response that half of the tracks will not be used on the eventual release, while the other half have "changed and evolved".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245"><span>[</span>245<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna eventually revealed the album, <i><a href="/wiki/Rebel_Heart_(Madonna_album)" title="Rebel Heart (Madonna album)">Rebel Heart</a></i>, and scheduled it for release on March 10, 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ggtheft_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-ggtheft-246"><span>[</span>246<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry">Artistry</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_themes_and_genres">Musical themes and genres</span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:30em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9; padding:8px">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"[Madonna] is a brilliant pop melodist and lyricist. I was knocked out by the quality of the writing [during <i>Ray of Light</i> sessions]. The lyrics to "<a href="/wiki/The_Power_of_Good-Bye" title="The Power of Good-Bye">The Power of Good-Bye</a>" are stunning. I love Madonna as an artist and a songwriter... I know she grew up on <a href="/wiki/Joni_Mitchell" title="Joni Mitchell">Joni Mitchell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Motown" title="Motown">Motown</a>, and to my ears she embodies the best of both worlds. She is a wonderful confessional songwriter, as well as being a superb hit chorus pop writer... She doesn’t get the credit she deserves as a writer."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—<a href="/wiki/Rick_Nowels" title="Rick Nowels">Rick Nowels</a>, who co-wrote with Madonna on <i>Ray of Light</i>, commented on her songwriting skill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247"><span>[</span>247<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>Madonna's music has been the subject of much analysis and scrutiny. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_McQueen_Grant" title="Robert McQueen Grant">Robert M. Grant</a>, author of <i>Contemporary Strategy Analysis</i> (2005), commented that what has brought Madonna success is "certainly not outstanding natural talent. As a vocalist, musician, dancer, songwriter, or actress, Madonna's talents seem modest."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSA_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-CSA-248"><span>[</span>248<span>]</span></a></sup> He asserts Madonna's success is in relying on the talents of others, and that her personal relationships have served as cornerstones to the numerous reinventions in the longevity of her career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSA_248-1"><a href="#cite_note-CSA-248"><span>[</span>248<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna's approach was far from the music industry wisdom of "Find a winning formula and stick to it." Her musical career has been a continuous experimentation with new musical ideas and new images and a constant quest for new heights of fame and acclaim. Grant concluded that "having established herself as the queen of popular music, Madonna did not stop there, but continued re-inventing."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249"><span>[</span>249<span>]</span></a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Musicologist" title="Musicologist">Musicologist</a> <a href="/wiki/Susan_McClary" title="Susan McClary">Susan McClary</a> wrote that "Madonna's art itself repeatedly deconstructs the traditional notion of the unified subject with finite ego boundaries. Her pieces explore various ways of constituting identities that refuse stability, that remain fluid, that resist definition."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250"><span>[</span>250<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Throughout her career, Madonna has been involved in writing and producing most of her own music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-music_credit_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-music_credit-251"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna's early songwriting skill was developed during her time with the <a href="/wiki/Breakfast_Club_(band)" title="Breakfast Club (band)">Breakfast Club</a> in 1979.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goldmine_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-goldmine-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> According to author Carol Gnojewski, her first attempts at songwriting are perceived as an important self-revelation, as Madonna said: "I don't know where [the songs] came from. It was like magic. I'd write a song every day. I said 'Wow, I was meant to do this'."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gnojewski57_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gnojewski57-252"><span>[</span>252<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mark_Kamins" title="Mark Kamins">Mark Kamins</a>, her first producer, believed that Madonna is "a much underrated musician and lyricist."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-morton20_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-morton20-253"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Rolling Stone</i> has named her "an exemplary songwriter with a gift for <a href="/wiki/Hook_(music)" title="Hook (music)">hooks</a> and indelible lyrics."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254"><span>[</span>254<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Freya Jarman-Ivens, Madonna's talent for developing "incredible" hooks for her songs allows the lyrics to capture the attention of the audience, even without the influence of the music. As an example, Jarman-Ivens cites the 1985 single "<a href="/wiki/Into_the_Groove" title="Into the Groove">Into the Groove</a>" and its line "Live out your fantasy here with me, just let the music set you free; Touch my body, and move in time, now I know you're mine."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fouz55_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-fouz55-255"><span>[</span>255<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna's songwriting are often autobiographical over the years, dealing with various themes from love and relationships to self-respect and female empowerment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256"><span>[</span>256<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257"><span>[</span>257<span>]</span></a></sup> Her songs also speak about taboo and unconventional issues of their period, such as sexuality and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS" title="AIDS">AIDS</a> on <i>Erotica</i> (1992).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258"><span>[</span>258<span>]</span></a></sup> Many of her lyrics contain innuendos and <a href="/wiki/Double_entendre" title="Double entendre">double entendre</a>, which lead to multiple interpretations among music critics and scholars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rikky_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-rikky-259"><span>[</span>259<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260"><span>[</span>260<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna was nominated for being inducted in the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame" title="Songwriters Hall of Fame">Songwriters Hall of Fame</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261"><span>[</span>261<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<table class="mbox-small-left" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;float:left">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><img alt="" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></div>
</div>
</td>
